Action Required: FYI

1. Attached is a book on revolutionary theory, "La Iglesia,
el Subdesarrollo y la Revolucion," recently published by
“Editorial Nuestro Tiempo" (which often publishes pro-Communist
material), which was brought to the Station's attention by
 LIBUFF-1 on 22 October 1968.

2. With the exception of one of the ten authors who
contributed to this book (Karl LENKERSDORF) all others subscribe,
in one way or another, to the developing thesis that Christian
(both Catholic and Protestant) theology justifies the use of
violence (i.e., killing if necessary) to bring about basic
structural changes in the "Third World." An undercurrent of
sympathy for revolutionary "martyrs" "Che" Guevara and Camilo
Torres permeates uost of the writings, as does the old favorite
shibboleth of Latin American "intellectuals" that the United
States has purposely kept Latin America underdeveloped (to
maintain a source of cheap raw materials and a market for
expensive manufactured goods).

Remove fron Project KOACEfeve.
izations SOMLYROS

HMMA-35792 6 November 1968

CASSIFICRTION
SECRET

|
|

DISPATCH [ees [=

saath tibetan



Cee eATON pureien Sewaae AND NUMEER

CONTINUATION OF
+ DISPATCH SECRIT HMMA-35792

3. In a strange marriage of "progressive" Catholic philosophy
with the old positivistic liberai tradition (which, by the way, was
quite anti-Catholic up to the days of the Mexican Revolution), this
pook addresses itself to well-documented statistical studies (mostly
produced under United Nations auspices) to state the case of Latin
American underdevelopment, and then proceeds to justify violent
revolution with Cnristian principles on the grounds that basic
needs for human subsistence have, been denied to the Latin American #
masses, The Thomistic principlesthat he who is starving may kill “eo
to get food is frcaichtIy auotéd; but no effort is made to define ~ #
“basic needs" i1 the modern world (obviously, millions of Latin af
Americans are not starving to death; and there is little agreement
on what constitutes "subsistence level"). Therefore, without
defining what are “indispensable needs," most of the authors agree
that basic structural changes are required to satisfy these
(undefined) needs, and proceed to the next step: this justifies
violent revolution.

4. The problem is that most of the authors depart from a
basically Marxist-positivist point of view: the assumption that
private enterprise is incompatible with social justice, and that
only a fundamentally socialistic economy can provide the infra-
structure for an equitable distribution of wealth.

5. Despite the verbosity of the writers, their message is
simple: (A) statistical analyses show two-thirds of the world is
starving and lacks "basic needs of human existence;" (B) history
shows that "The Establishment" will not give in to reason; 7
(C) divine natural law stipulates that man has an overriding right
to satisfy his basic needs; (D) since "The Establishment" will not i
give in to reason, divine natural law authorizes violent revolution |
to establish an “equitable distribution of wealth." But what '
system would follow violent revolution to insure equitable distri-
bution? The Marxist bias of the authors comes forth, Tomas G.
ALLAZ, French Dominican priest who teaches at the Seminario de
Leon, Gto., Mexico, frankly quotes with approval a famous passage
from "L'Osservatore Romano" of 8 May 1949: "Communism as such,
that is, as an economic system, leaving aside its philosophy, is i
not against the very nature of Christianism as much as, is i
capitalism." In another passage, Father ALLAZ also exemplifies
the authors’ anti-U.S. bias: “Children in Vietnam are cut to
pieces by the bombs of the Good Samaritans of the world.”
Communist terror is nowhere mentioned. The book, therefore,
appears to be essentially an effort to justify with Christian , ;
theology Fidel CASTRO's call to arms against the status quo in * :
Latin America. 7

6. Index book authors, "Che" Guevara, and Camilo Torres.

for/Willard C. CURTIS

LIHUFF Progress Report/ 1 July 1967 through 31 May 1968

[ACTON RTQUIRED. REFERENCES

REFERENCE: A. HMMA~34773
B, HMMNA-34757

tai te ite

1. During the past year the main activities of this project
(which consists of only LIHUFF/1, a WOLADY citizen contract agent)

have been aimed at:

a) Procuring reports on right wing political groups and
right-wing student organizations. These data are obtained by
LIHUFF/1 from LICHANT/1 and LIHUFF/2, both of whom are non-
paid contacts of LIHUFF/1.

ce etieane hae

b) The use of M.U.R.O, extreme right wing Catholic
student organization, principally at tue Universidad Nacional;
Autonoma de Mexico (UNAM), with branches in several provincial

univerisities.

c) The use of LIHUFF/1 to make (business) organization
traces through Dun and Bradstreet and similar groups. LIHUFF/1
and his organization (through LIHUFF/1) are also used to
procure background, operational and investigative data needed

by the Station.

nomic atdeh ake

cease dane

2. EFFECTIVENESS:
Some examples of the work done by LIHUFF/1 are cited below:

a) Some forty (40) Dun and Bradstreet reports were
obtained during the period on individuals and/or organizations ;

of interest to this Station.
t

b) During this period LIHUFF/1 provided the Station
with details of Mexican Government plans to impose legisla~
tive restrictions on foreign investments and of Mexican
Government orders to Mexican Banks to limit loans to private
corporations with an appreciable amount of foreign capital.
(Note: This proved of particular interest to the Embassy).

OSL IHUFE Progress Report | July through 31 October 1966

‘ACTION FEGURED -REFTRONCES

Reference: HMMW-14683 dated 24 June 1966

i 1, The LIKUFF project was last approved on 18 June 1966 for
the period | July 1966 through 30 June 1967 for a budget of U.S.
dollars $4,200.00. This project provides the Chief of Station Mexico
with a source (LIHUFF*1) who has access to right-wing organizations
in Mexico, including a student action group at the Universidad

Nacional Autonoma de Mexico (UNAM) known as Movimiento Universitario
de Renovadora Orientacion (MURO).

2. Summary of Project Activity.

a. This project provided the Station with a copy of
a manuscript of the first half of a book on communism written by
Father Baldomero OROTONEDA Comas, a Jesuit priest assigned to
this task by his order. Though the reviewing officers at the
Mexico Station felt that the manuscript contained no information
useful for the Station's operational program, a microfilm was
transmitted to Headquarters for more detailed review and recom=
mendations (HMMA-29365 dated 5 July 1966).

b. During this reporting period, LIHUFF-1 reported
regularly on the situation at the UNAM and while this information
did not result in positive intelligence disseminations, it was

useful for background purposes.

c. During July 1966 the LIHUFF student organization,
with the help of Senator Alfonso GUERRA of Nayarit, initiated a
press campaign against the Czech Embassy and the Commercial Office |
in Mexico, singling out for attack Emil HRADECKY (201-204658),

~cont inued=

REFERENCE: EMI-10,841, 16 November 1966

Referenced report, entitled
Disturbances at the University of Michoscan, Morelia, Hichoacan",
include

cle exposing the Central Nacional de Estudiontes
Democraticos (CXED) of being nothing more than a dependency of the
Mexican Communist Party (PCH). A coment on the cover sheet to that
report stated that a member of the HURO, using a faked PCH carpet,
had caused the arti-le to be published,

2. The Station now knovs from the LITEMPOs and LINUFF~1 that a
MURO member did, in fact, go to the offices of §1 Universal and using
his faked PCM carnet Plunked down the necessary money (approxiuately.
21,150 MN) and had the article printed. The purpose of the operation
was to try to discredtt the CNED just prior to its nation] meeting
held in Konterrey on 17, 18 nnd 19 Novenber 1966, While most people
in the PCH, the CNED and other organizations controlled by, or ba
affiliated with the PCM are aware that the PCM controls the CNED,
many of the organizations and members of the CNED in the interior of
the country and the Mexican public ip &eneral are not aware of PCH
control and influence in the CKED

sernpetngevertt

3. Although there is no indication that the article had any
adverse effect on the CNED meeting in Monterrey, it ts clear that the F
was disturbed about it and took steps to bring action against El
Universal, accusing this newspaper formally of trying to damage the
yeputation of the PCH and the CNED. La Voz de Kexico, issue number
1857, 20 November 1866, carried an article on the front page which
stated that on 17 November 1566 Arnoldo MARTINEZ Verdugo, First
Secretary of the PCH, made a formal accusation against Fl Universal
to the Attorney-General of the Republic, and it added that “It is.
hoped that the authorities will take the appropriate action". .
LITEMPO-8 has since told CCS that they (the Mexican Government) were

well aware of the operation, approved of it, and that no action will
be taken against the newspaper,

Reference:

1, Reference A is incorrectly titled. There is no “LIHUFF
Student Subsidy" -- and the payments given to this group were and
are for specific jobs done at Station (and in one case at Chief

LNPURE) specific request.

2, Station requests for specific actions are put to the student
group, via LIHUFF/1, and from him to LIHUFF/2, This student group
happens to be one which will take direct and even physical actions
against communists.

3. Specifically, this student group:

a. Caused the termination of a Chinese Communist Art Exhibit
at UNAM by their direct action,’ and this was done at Station request
as a result of a request of Chief LNPURE.

b. Paraded on 23 October 1966 with a black coffin and
signs in front of the Soviet and Cuban Embassies in mourning over
Soviet mis-treatment of Hungary in commemoration of the Anniversary
of the Hungarian Uprising.

c. Put a full-page advertisement in "El Universal", on
10 November 1966, which Bi fegedly came from a Communist Party member.
This student group made a (false) carnet for a student group member

with his photograph on it, and convinced this highly reputable

caused quite a sensation in communist circles. It also "blew"

e. Other anti-communist operations.

4, COS, Mexico City, does not intend to commit a specific
amount to the LIHUFF Student Group but, when specific operations
are desired and are given to this group to do, it is intended that
they will be paid for the operation or given sums from LILISP/X
to pay towards the expenses of these (specific) operations.

5. Payments are made for jobs accomplished and not in advance.
This is believed to be a completely justifiable use of LILISP/X

LUHUFF

1. On 24 October 1966, the Mexico City News, English language
daily, reported that approximately 200 students and members of the
Movimiento Universitario de Renovadora Orientacion (MURO), extreme
right wing organization, had gathered in front of the Soviet Embassy
on Sunday, 23 October, to commemorate the 10th anniversary of the
crushing of the Hungarian rebellion. The demonstration was broken
up by police but not before the students had placed a casket at the
entrance to the Soviet Embassy, and covered the sidewalk area with
banners and wreaths protesting the Soviet action in Hungary,

2. Some of the students formed another group and marched
to the Cuban Embassy wher: the police took into custody some 36 of.
the marchers. They were taken to the police headquarters, given a
lecture on the requirement for a permit to make such a "march" and
released, Among those arrested was Fernando Bafios Urquijo, President
of KURO. No students were held by the police.

3. LIHUFF/1 advised COS, Mexico City, on 26 October 1966,
that he and LIHUFF/2 had planned the “march" and were very proud
of their success and the publicity resulting from it. tae)

4, Enclosed are copies of press clippings from tecal daily

newspapers.
Aailiard c. CORMISK

Students Stage

Hungary Revolt March

Police Break Up Demonstration

Student groups marching on the
Soviet and Cuban embassies yesterday
to commemorate the 10th anniversary
of the crushing of the Hungarian re-
bellion were broken up by police,

About. 200 members of the Univer-
sity New Orientation Movement (MU.
RO) were dispersed in front of the
Soviet Embassy after they laid a cas.
ket at the main entrance.

The National University (UNAM)

the Soviet action in Budapest. They
hung them on the iron fence in front
of the embassy and laid wreaths on
_ the sidewalk,

students carried banners protesting -

| At Russian, Cuban Embassies

When the marchers were broken
up at the Soviet Embassy, they tried
fo regroup to march on the Cuban
Embassy. They were met there by a
large police force,

Police arrested 36 MURO members
at the Cuban Embassy.. They were
taken to police headquarters and
freed after being lectured on their
conduct. .

Among those arrested were Fer.
nando Bahos Urquijo, head of MURO,
and other movement leaders.

Both the Soviet and Cuban embas-
sles declined fo comment on the in-
eldent.

El expresado desarrollo o crecimiento economico, que re-

admite por regla general que el fomento de relaciones pacifi-
cas en este turbulento y dindmico mundo en que vivimos re-
quicre el desarrollo econémico de todos los paises, en especial
de nquélios donde prevalecen todavia condiciones de vida pre-
domtinantemente rurales. E] desarrollo de los paises que fue-
ron anteriormente colonias y de otros pafses industrialmente
‘atrasados es absolutamente necesario para que se produzca
un desarrollo sano de las naciones avanzadas, ya que las eco-
ins industrinles mantienen su crecimiento y estabilidad

‘nol c "

cinkes.

De todas las condiciones requeridas para cl incremento
de Jos ingresos en los paises rurates del mundo, las que ocu-
pan una posicién estratégica decisiva son un erecimiento con-
tinuado, estable y saludable de los principales pafses indus-
trinles y In eliminacion en estos paises de toda prolongada con-
traccidn o estancamiento econdmico. Cualquier idea de ace-
lerar el crecimiento de los paises aubdesarrollades mediante
el debilitamiento de las naciones industriales pertenece & la
apolillada mentalidad del determinismo marxista y al espejis-
mo. del “paraiso de tos prolctarios” regido por dictudura.
Desde que estas grandes ideas han sido ensayadas durante
casi cuarenta afios en un experimento de Jaboratorio con va-
rios centenares de millones de personas, han perdido su brillo
y su atrayente colorido.

Las economfas de los pafses industriales y de los que 56
hallan en vias de desarrollo se encuentran actualmente en
una situacién de mutua interdependencia, como lo esta asi-
nusmo el mantenimiento de la convivencia pacifica entre jas
naciones. Los paises industrinles necesitan una corriente ade
cuada y creciente de productos primarios de loa pafses en vias
de desarollo, y pagarin por cllos, al igual que por los articu-

Una nueva concepciin del intercambio internacional:
el efecto Prebisch

A fin de comprender Ia situacién ambigua y confusa que
predomina actualmente en las capitales de las naciones indus-
trializadas de Occidente, trataré de esbozar a grandes lineas

algunas do las ideas que dominaron las discusiones de la Con- -

ferencia de Ginebra. Los representantes de muchos paises
en desarrollo aceptaron como una nueva especie de ley natu-
ral inmutable el Hamado “efecto Prebisch”, que atribuye la
debilidud de las balanzas de pagos de los paisea exportadores
de productos primarios al deterioro de los términos de inter-
cambio. Desde esta perspectiva, los remedios aconsejables
serfan los siguientes:

_ Lies paises en desarrollo deben industrializarse con to-
da rapidez. Para lograrlo, deben abandonar el principio de Jas
vontajas compnrativas y aceptar, como precio de ln industria-
lizacién, costos superiores, en vez de inferiores, de los pro-

worl

pperenegnaees rr oem per tne maya Se cee son a etree tamara wan nin na



aint Randi atubeaadn,, «| Foie = stented te ann

ductos industriales. En consecuencia, deben proteger sus in-
dustrias; dicha proteccién puede Hlevarse a cabo mediante
aranceles aduancros, impuestos a la importacién o cualquier
otro medio. Con el propdsito de fortalecer dicho proteccio-
nismo, los pafses en vias de desarrollo deben agruparse y coris-
tituir uniones aduaneras con aranceles exteriores comunes
elevados.

2. Simultdncamente, los palses industriales deben conce-
der trato preferenclal para ly entrada de exportaciones de
productos primarios de los paises en desarrollo a precios “ade-
cuados”, es decir, a precios remunecradores para los exporta-
dores,

3. A fin de Impedir que los precios de los productos pri-
marios caigun por debajo de un minimun convenido, los paf-
des en desarrotlo deben imponer impuestos de cuantia varia-
ble sobre In exportaciin de las materias primarias, proporcio-
nales, en caso necesario, a una escala previamente fijada,

4. Todos los pafses deben estabilizar los precios de las
materias primas a un nivel beneficioso para los pafses expor-
tadores mediante convenios internacionales sobre mercancias,
asf como constituir reservas amortiguadoras y asignar cuo-
tas de-exportacién a los pafses en vias de desarrollo.

5. Los paises, industriales deben suministrar una corrien-
te sustancialmenie mayor de capitales a los paises en desa-
rrollo.

Mucho se puede afiadir o suprimir a este atrevido proyec-
to de reorganizucién total de la actual estructura institucional
del comercio internacional y del financiamiento para el des-
arrollo. Pero si las naciones industriales aceptaran, aunque
sélo fuera parcialnente, Ja filosofia que impregna este pro-
yecto, la consecuencia seria la ivuvitable paralizacién de una
parte considerable de ias fuerzas que otorgan a las economias
de los pafses industrializados y de una serie de pafses en de-
sarrollo, basadas en las decisiones descentralizadas de la eco-
nomfa de mecado, su enorme dinamismo y su poderosa elas-
ticidad.

comin: Suponen que la institucién a escala mundial de un

Quisiera aludir aqui a una de las refaciones de precios de
eartcter mis estratégico para la politica agricola y alimenti-
¢la mundiel, La produccién de una tonelada de abono nitro-

1, The attached material relating to the establishment of "public awareness"
officials in U.S. businesses in Latin America was passed to COS by
LIHUFF-1, As can be seen from the correspondence between LIHUFF-1

and Mr, Smithies of the Council for Latin America Inc, regarding this
matter, the Council will attempt to interest U.S, parent companies in this
program. According to LIHUFF-1, the Council will also approach
Undersecretary of State Thomas Mann and his assistant, Robert Adama,

in line with LIHUFF-l's suggestion in his letter of 26 July 1965.

2. The attached correspondence and related material is being forwarded
with the request that it be passed to Robert Adams in anticipation of an
approach to his office by the Council for Latin America along the above

garding the establishment of “public awareness" officials
in U.S, business firms in Latin America, According to Mr.
Wichtrich, the Council for Latin America also intends to
appreach Under Secretary Mann for support in launching this

1, Ina letter to LIHUFF/1 dated 16 June 1965, LIHUFF/2 reported the
following:

The Escuela Nactonal de Economia of the Universidad Nacional Autor
de Mexico (UNAM) has organized a program of summer courses in which
various Mexican and foreign professors have been invited to participate.
According to a circular issued by the UNAM, the following program of
courses was planned: 14 June: Prof. Michal Kalacki, Professor of the
Central School of Planning and Statistics in Warsaw, on the subj:ct
"Financing Economic Development in Mixed Economies." 15 June: Prof.
Joan Robinson of the University of Cambridge, England, on "The New Wave
in the Science of Economica." 16 June: Professor Arthur Smithies of
Harvard University, on "The Structured Polemic." 18 June: Prof.

Arthur Smithies, on a subject to be determined. 18 June: Round table
discussion with the following professors participating: Joan Robinson,
Michal Kalacki, Arthur Smithies, Horacio Flores de la Pefia, Jose Luis
Cecefia, Alonso Aguilar, Efigenia M. de Navarrete and Josue Saenz.

2. The above was reported by LIHUFF/1 to COS on 18 June, Station
information on the local Comnunist contacts of Joan Robinson hag been

nd Headquarters,

1__Specific ~ LINUFF Progress Report for February through March 1965
"ACTION REQUIRED - REFERENCES

XX__| aicrorin H

1.

The major occurrence during this period has been the reorganization of the
LIMUPF student organization. An entirely new board of directors was placed
at the head of the organization in’ March. The names of the old and new
board of directors@¥: indicated in the neve item forvarded as Separate Cover
Attachment No, 1. In addition thereto, as will be noted below, the

board of directors of the LIHUFY student organization was reorganized at the
University of Puebla during thia period,

2, Other major activities during this period have been the following:

a, The LIHUFF student organization put out enother issue of its student
publication, copy of which is forwarded as Separate Cover Attachment No. 2.
LIHUFF/2 reported that 1000 copies of this publication were sold in a single
morning in the UNAM School of Law.

b. The new board of directors of the LIHUFF student group at the University
of Puebla was installed on 25 March. This was part of a reorganization under-
taken et that university due to che fact that the latter has continued to
Slip further and further into the hands of far leftists. LIWUFF/2 noted

that the particular danger at this university is in the two faculties of
economy and philosophy since they are drawing Comunist-oriented professors
from UNAM whose study programs and plans are drawn up accordingly. LINUFF/2
also indicated that with the situation as it is in Puebla there will be a

need for greater economic assistance there.

Cerca del Istmo de la Trivialidad, en el Mar de la ‘Apatia, la nave‘de la patria se hundia fe
lenta e Inexorablemente en el olvido, , : - t

A bordé, la mayoria de los pasajeres y de la tripulacién estaban acostades al sol como L
de costumbre. Sobre la probabilidad inmedista de ahogarse, habla varios grados de conciencia, :
También habia dos érdenes de pensamientos sobre Ia materia, Un pequelio grupo insistia no ax: |
lamente en que si se bundia la nave, en realidad, esto era malo. Otro pequefio grupo inistin en’. i
que era perfectamente correct que se hundiera la nave, y es més, en que los pasajeros progre: !
sistas, comunistas, socialistas, que miraban hacia el futuro, debfan ayudar a que esto suecdiera.
Las olas que sumergian la nave eran simplemente “las olas del futuro..."

Sa
Miembros de este Gltimo grupo estaban callada pero sisteméticamente taladrando aguje
ros en el fondo del bareo para apresurar y asegurar el hundimiento de! mismo: alrededor de ecte.
grupo de conspiradores estaba un grupo much més grande y ruideso que defendia con sofis |
mas y falasias, los actos de estos que taladraban desde adentro, Sus explicaciones mis eomunes :
eran que:

~ " Primero—Los conspiradores no sstaban realmente dafiando el bareo sino aumentando su |
“seguridad porque los agujeros taladrados eran para permitir que el agua que ya estaba dentro |
de la nave fluyera hacia fuera; y

Segundo.—z Qué importa después de a TAl fin y al cabo na shogadita nunca le
hizo dafio a nadiel...*

En la proa del barco otro grupo pequefio elevaba sus oraciones, pidiendo la intervencién |

divina,., un esfuerzo loable. Pero precisamente entre ellos, uno de los conspiradores taladraba |
asfduamente, y el grupo de fieles no hacia nada para impedirlo, :



2 een edna enema emacs

~ gm otra Grea protegida y confortable, hhabfe otro grupo, éste, una aglvnetacién de teori-

upatan de cuazdo er cucnde con debaves acaiorades aceraa de ia Be

clolégica y la sabiduria econémica de taladrar agujeros en el fondo del bareo. Finalmente cada

discusién terminaba con un acuerdo general que este procedimiento carecia de bases sélidas, y

el grupo acordaba firmar una resolucién en ese sentido para que fuera publieada en el periddico

del barca, Entre dis.wriéa y discusién se ocupaban de otros asuntos académicos de importancia,
tales ‘como la historia de la perforacién de agujeros en las armadas del pasado.

Sovre los mastues estaba encaramado or» grupo numeroso de personas que trataba de
ignorarlo todo, Todos ellos esperaban que un viento politico empujara al barco hacia la playa
antes de que se hundiera, Desgraciadamente todos los vientos politicos soplaban hacia altamar
y no habia tierra a la vista. aie ! :

i
~ La mayoria de los oficiales del bareo estaban muy ocupados escribiendo y entregando 1io-
tas a los conspiradores, ofreciéndoles taladros ms grandes, para que hicieran agujeros mas gram
des, para-que pudieran sacar toda esa agua desagradable del barco con la mayor rapider.

En el centro del barco habia un grupo pequeiio de pasajeros que dirigia el Capitin, de-
dicados a la tarea de impedir el hundimiento. Algugos de este grupo se esforzaban en hacer fun-
cionar las borabas. Otros trataban de tapar los agujeros de: més ripido posible y en esta ope
racién recibian tremendas embarradas de lodo y mugre, Otros frataban de aprehender s los cons.
piradores para meterlos en la cArcel del bareo,’ pero sus esfuerzos se velan obstaculizados por su
escaso nimero, y por los cuerpos de la gente dormida, sobre los cuales tenian que pasar. De vez
en cuando alguno de estos pasajercs dormidos habria un ojo y decia: “Sé que ‘deberia Ree
Pero no me gustan sus métodos”.

El espectéculo m4s curioso y a la vez més patético lo presentaban sin embargo, unas per-
sonas que ya sabian que el barco se hurdia, que. ya estaban en la mar, y que apenas alcanzaban
8 gritar entre las-marejadas: “;Puedo luchar mejor independientemente!” _

Nuestra Coustitucién Mexicana. -

El nuevo gobierno de-la Republica ha promulgado como su meta la PLENA VIGENCIA de?

la Constitucién Mexicana y ha hecho un paneginco de la libertad, ieee

La Constitucién Mexicana tiene un dia sefialado en el calendario para celebrar su promul-

res pacion. Fue un verdadero acontecimiento registrado ya para siempre en los anales de nuestra

Desde el punto de vista politico, la Constitucién establecié tres poderes: Ejecutivo, Legislati-
vo y Judicial. Ello tenia por fin que la separacion de dichos tres poderes garantizara el bienestar *
social e individual,

Desde el punto de vista econémico, la Constitucién en su Articulo 28 establecié el sistema de !
libertad econdémica, Basie
MECANISMO DE LA LIBERTAD ECONOMICA

El Articulo 28 de la-Constitucién de los Estados Unidos Mexicanos, dice:

“Articulo 28—En los Estados Unidos Mexicanos no habré monopolios ni estancos de nin-
= clase; NI EXENCION DE IMPUESTOS; ni prohibiciones a titulo de proteccidn a la indus-

la oe violar este articulo Constitucional.

DERECHO DE PROPIEDAD i

Pero todo lo anterior no tendria sentido, si el derecho de propiedad no estuviera también
garantizado,

Por edo la Constituciéa garantiza el derecho de propiedad en su articulo 14 cuando dice:

s NADIE PODRA SER PRIVADO DE.LA VIDA, DE LA LIBERTAD O DE SUS PROPIE-
PADES LUSESIONES 0 DERECHOS, sino mediante juicio sepuido ante los Tribunales nretorrne

~ {g,qstablecidos, en el que se cumplan las formalidades esenciales del procedimiente y onfern a
las leyes expecidas con anterioridad al hecho".

Todavia més, el Articulo 16 dices,
“NADIE PUEDE SER MOLESTADO EN SU PERSONA, FAMILIA, DOMICILIO, PAPE.

LES 0 FOSESIONES, sino en virtud de mandamiento escrito de la autoridad competente: gies for
de y motive ia causa legal del procedimiento”. ae

: Todo control, todo monopolio, todo impedimento para que cualquiera persona pueda gozur wv.
Ja libertad econdmica garantizada por la Constitucién, ES ANTICONSTITUCIONAL. f

NINGUNA AUTORIDAD PUEDE VIOLAR LA CONSTITUCION, y sélo los jueces pueden,
* en casos muy particuiares, coartar dicha libertad. eats

A pesar de todo, la libertad ecanémica consagrada por la Constitucién ha sido victima de
muchos ataques,

: Existen controles, subsidios, exenciones de impuestos, y muchos otros impedimentos para
gozar de una plena libertad econémica. Todos esos impedimentos, ademis de ir contra la ley ma-
3ima que nos rige, atentan contra nuestra propia libertad, porque la libertad no pulede ser pancat
¥ la falta de libertad en materia econémica es un atentado contra la propia liberiad indideek

Confiadamente esperamos que en esta ocasién SI se cumpla con la Constitucién.
(Reproduceién de 1a Hoja de Informacién Econémica No. 1 dei 15 de Mayo de 1955),

POR VICTOR RICO GALAN

El Arzobispo Primado de Méxi-
co, Monsefior Miguel Dario Mi-
randa, dirigié a los fieles relacio-
nados con la educaciéh una car-
ta desautorizando al Movimiento
Universitario de Renovadora
Orientacién, enrevesado nombre
que tiene por objeto formar con
sus iniciales la palabra MURO.
Desde hace tiempo, el MURO ha
venido actuando en los medios estudiantiles en una forma
que sélo puede ser calificada de canallesca. Su principal
actividad aparente es la delacién, que usa para extorsio-

nar a todos aquellos que no se le someten. Se supone que
cuantes son ajencs a las actividades extremamente secta-
rias de] MURO, son comunistas, y como tales se les exhibe
en la picota.

Por otra parte, el MURO ejerce la violencia contra
aquellos estudiantes que no lo apoyan. Hay que suponer
que a estas formas de extorsién que han trascendido al
pdblico, se suman otas menos conocidas, pero no menos
inmorales y delictuoscs. De una organizacién que ha le-
gado al extremo de Zamar comunisia al padre dominico
Tomds Allaz, puede esperarse todo. El Primado de Méxi-
co dice en su carta muy claramente que “se aparta de las
directrices de la Iglesia y aun a veces de la misma ley mo-
ral, que debe normar todas las acciones humanas para
que sean licitas y bendecidas por Dios”.

En realidad, el MURO es una organizacién tipicamen-
te fascista. Pretende imponer a todo trance una ideologia
eavernicola, y no retrocede ante la extorsién ni la violen-
cia Hsica para lograrlo. Nada tiene, en el fondo, de caté-
lica ni de cristiana. Pero se cobija bajo el manto de la
religién, porque ka. goles. la mayoria de los mexicanos ¥
espera con eso obtener la popularidad que, por su propia
naturaleza, le est4 vededa. Un viejo truco. Un viejo y po-
drido truco.

Traer a Dios a la pelea callejera, con la macana o la
cadena, es la peor injuria que se le puede hacer. Ningun
ezistimo auténtico podria admitir semejante cosa, pero

sur iaseeese sense, panseaseSeeeenauseeusensqenguece’ Jaue’ J2tase

Y obligen a ios no catélicos a dudes del respeto que imere- 4

Ce tode creyente verdadero. Pretender que Dios es militan-
te de una causa politica determineda perjudica a los caté- .
licos antes que a nadie, porque equivale a darle lal jerar-
quia de la politica que se deliende. Puede admitir frco

tolico verdadero que Dios tenga esa jerurquia, o

otra reservada en el fondo de sa corazén?

manifestar, no sélo Ja falta de solidaridad de la Igh me- 5

erganismo fascistoide. Y es bueno hacer constar que eso
indica una saludable evolucién en Ia jerarquia eclesidstica j

POR ROBERTO BLANCO MOHENO

La noche anterior a mi salida de Chi-
huahua, cuando comentaba con Javier
Palacio el horror de aquella situacion, la
imposibilidad de dejar de ser “peripa-
tético” ante el vicio'y el crimen herma.
nados para robar a un pueblo, ta dolo-
Yosa necesidad de desafinar con amargas
verdades cuando todo el periodisme na-
cional forma el coro de las alabanzas,
una voz querida me dijo, desde México:

—Llegd un telegrama del general
Cardenas.

iDios! No cabe duda de que en la
vida existen las compensaciones. Porque
tenia en las manos, todavia, el olo. mal-
dito de la prision en que se mueren to-
dos Jos dias Rios, Cardona y Rodriguez
F.; porque la cronica indignacién se me
hacia un pozo doloroso ante la miseria
indeseriptible de aquella buena gente, y
el valor sacrificado de los estudiantes,
y_ia iterminable soledad del yermo de
Chihvabua, donde no viven ni siquiera
Jagartijas. El nombre de Cardenas, egoistamente, me hace olvidar, por
un momento no mas, la rabia impotente que me muerde el alma. Se
me permitira —lo permitira usted, Pepe Pagés— decir que al escu-
char el texto de ese telegrama siento tas entrafias todas del alma
lavadas y hallo, en un camina a cada dia mas duro, nuevas fuerzas
hacidas directamente de la mano de ese hombre maravilloso que es
don Lazaro. Si don Lazaro se pincha un dedo —Io digo con el mismo
derecho, y el mismo fervor, con que he dicho sobre él algunas inev.
tables amargas verdades— de ese dedo no sale sangre... jsale Me.
xico!

Biaxe¢ Moneno

Haria un mes que habia mandado un mensaje a Ciudad Alta
uno de los centros vitales de la Comisién del Balsas, dicién-

dole a Cardenas que si era todavia oportuno, me Sustaria conocer la
verdadera situacién de la zona guerrerense y michoacana afectada por
Jos recientes temblores para ver la manera de hacer Hegar al Presi-
dente Lépez Mateos, patio de todas las lagrimas, las necesidades que
les seores gobernadores tienen la costumbre de no ver, ciegos casi
todos a puro egoismo. Cuando pasaron las semanas y de Cindad Al.
tamirano nada legd, senti un poco de mordedura del despecho. Es
cierto que he dicho en estas paginas mi condena del a CCI y de sus
dirigentes comunistas —aunque no legé a insultarlos como los pro-
pios campesinos de esa Central hace unos dias, en que los echaron
ignominiosamente—; es verdad que acedi a dos Teuniones de los diri-
gentes del Movimiento de Liberacién Nacional, entre los cuales desta-
caban Cuaubtémoe Cardenas, Alonso y Gonzilez Pedrero, y que me
Tetiré indignado ante la absurda postura, la inmovilidad y hasta la
cobardia que encontré: y algo mas grave: tuve necesidad, en mi libre
“El Cardenismo”, de ahondar en algunas cosas que forzosamente do-
Heron al gran michoacano. Pero no queria, no podia creer que el
Expropiador del Petroleo, el Padre agrarista, el campeén del Derecho
Internacional sufriera la mezquina enfermedad que padecen nuesires
intelectuales rojos. ;Si hay un hombre al que nunca debe Ilamarsele
intelectual, dado el giro que la palabrita ha tomado de quienes asi
se Haman, ese hombre es Cardenast Y ahora escuchaba el texto
del mensaje que muy poco después iba a revelarme la grandezs de
México y Ix miseria de México, toda la enorme y dolorosa paradoja
que es este formidable pais: “Recibi con enorme retraso tu mensoje
Porque no esture aqui. Senis bienvenido cuando quieras’. No quis.
to, Pepe Pages, aumento de sueldo: iya estoy pagado 10 suficiente!

*.

corazén de esta desolada region, de pobreza subhumana, sin recursos,
pues si bien es cierto que “no hay tierra mala con agua” aqui no, hay
tierra, sino tequesquite, piedra, tepetate, erosion, se levanta un :pue-
biito viejo en su anénimo dolor, en su hambze de siglos: se lathaba
Mariscala de Iturbide. Algo ha ganado, en un sentido moral, porque
a Ja fecha se ama Mariscala de Juarez. E} que escribe confiesal que

1, Background.
rum Iwi’ See y be wnson at

a. LIHUFF (Identity 1) was fainded in 1953 by a group of Mexican
businesemen to spread the principles of free enterprise and private initiative.
Since then, it has established ‘wumerous influential contacts and relationships
and engaged in a number of anti-Communist and other activities, It has neld
meetings of various types and congresse! n which the dangers of Communism
was the central theme; it has published books, pamphlets, and aewsletters on :
Communism ag well a the dangers of economic socialism;4t has organizeda_
student group (Identity 2)/"{t fas established and maintained Latin American :
contacts in the student and economic/business fields; it has engaged in con- :
siderable press placement on various matters involving private initiative and

the Communist threat; ami it has accumulated a file of basic data cn event and
individuals revolving about Communiem and Socialism that would be difficult for
any private Mexican group to duplicate, ‘This is quite aside from the many :
individuals, such as LICHANT), who have gravitated to LIHUFF and present j
various types of capabilities in the press, publishing, and eimilar fields.] 4
j

b. LIHUFF and its sponsors are considered in terms of the Mexican
scene as extreme right-wing conservatives; however, on the PBPRIME scene
they would be considered more as cent.ists, The importance of such a group,
vocal and combative, existing in Mexico, is not in absdute terms but in relative
terms. As is known by Headquarters, the ruling Partido Revolucionario
Inetitucional (PR1) party is basically a delicate reflector of the many political
currents and pressures that exist in Mexico. In elections, appointments and
decisions, the PRI cabal weighs very carefully all political equities, If only the
extreme leftists are vocal and active, then the decisions tend to be weighted
in their favor and oriented toward their wewpoint, In so many words, in order (/d-

¢

to keep some kind of counterbalance, even though tending towards extremes, ‘ &

the right mugt be as vocal and active as the left, Essentially, this is where |
the Station sees the value of the UFF mechanism, It does not expect Mexico

ever to revert to the LIHUFF philosophy or objectives en totoor even to any 5
very great degree; it does expect LIHUFF to exercise an influence and restraint [|

on Mexi uccumbing to the pressures and demands of the far left. Unless
some feW like LIHUFF/2 ‘aid Miguel ALEMAN Valdes were active through

organizations of their type, the political center of gravity would move further
towards the far left unchecked and further than ODYOKE policy would care +>
see it. This is the unique and specific value that this Station has seen, and
continues to see, in the LIHUFF activity.

eee
c, In mid-1960, on the strength of a LHUFF/2 contact with HBFINGH,
the Chief HBFINCH (Mexico) requested the Station to consider support of the
LIHUFF activity. A check with Headquarters indicated that KUBARK had been
Providing some support to LINUFF through Idertify'3, "Dut inasmuch as Identity 3
had died shortly before, the Station was asked by Headquarters to pick up the
funding. The Station funding initially was directed to Identity’3, the major.
regular publication of LIHUFF. A project was submitted by the Station in
reference C, but reference D indicated the project had been disapproved in the
form submitted, that support to Identi#*+-should be discontinued, and that
instead, the Station funds should be applied to the student activity (Identity 2) #40!
on a spot assistance basis, This was dong with PBPRIME business associates
of LIHUFF/I picking up the cost of Identity“# some $1,200 (US) per month.
At the present time, therefore, Station expenditures are confined to LIHUFF/1
salary ($500 per month) and $500 per month to Identity,2~~At this juncture aad
, the LIHUFF activity is costing $12, 0v0 per year.
The Station, however, retains access to the full range of the LINUFF mechanism
and potential.

;

2, Target. :

The major target insofar ae KUBARK funding is concerned is the
student field through Identity’<.° As is obvious, however, the LIHUFF mechanism
is available and used for other activities as well, An example is the Identity 5
book by LICHANT/I and the reference D request for another LICHANT/1
publication on Cuban refugees. LIHUFF/I and LIHUFF/2 increasingly provide
disseminable intelligence reports on political and student matters gathered
from their wide range of contacts, This is quite aside from a great deal ‘of
opezational information of value to the Station which does not merit dissemination,

3. Control,
Station access to, and control of, this activity depends primarily oa
the relationship of LIHUFF/1 with LINUFF/2. Precisely what percentage of
Fee ca ar | ea ne EAR Soman of Metaown tome fe

t

however, it is known that PBPRIME business men are underwriting Identity 4”
to the extent of $1200 (US) per month. The circulars and other activities
sustained by LIHUFF must involve, conservatively, another $1200 (US) per
month, The $500 (US) per month funded to LIHUFF by the Station, while
maintaining access and certainly providing useful support to LIHUFF in the
student field, cannot be considered control insurance in this situation,

Essentially, Station funds assure accees for LIHUFF/1 to LIHUFF/2 on unurt
matters and, with this entree, LIHUFF/] on the strength of their personal
relationship provides the control factor. Basically, the control factor is
probably guaranteed more by the personal relationship than the funds, In any
event, the control over LIHUFF activities is not absolute and, even given
complete funding of LIHUFF by KUBARK, would not be absolute, Possibly,

it could be improved a little more with some more funds, but not much,

This is because LIHUFF/2 is successful, prominent, capable and invdved with ;
too many other prominent people and events on his own to ever have any single :
individual or entity dictate his activities, attitudes, and soon, He ie responsive
to Station requirements on the use of Station funds and even seeks advice on
other LIHUFF activities not funded by the Station, What he is not readily
responsive to is detailed written reporting. He will give oral reports and
some written reports, Part of the problem in this regard undoubtedly is that
he is involved in so many activities that he finds it difficult to find the time.
For Station purposes in this particular program, the control is less than ideal
but certainly adequate for getting things done in the areas desired since there
is little question about his motivation and ability.

meen

t -
58 Relationship to Other Projects.

ee a, LICOAX: As indicated in reference B, both Project LICOAX and!
are operating in UNAM, a university of upwards of 80,000 students.
Thos far, there has been no problem of conflict since one is working the

Catholic side of the street and the other, the so-called "independents" --and
there is still plenty of room for both to operate, In this connection, it should :
be noted that a great deal of LIHUFF student effort is devoted to several ay

universities outside Mexico City; in other words, the UNAM is just one aspect.

b. LISIREN: This project is concerned with a mass propaganda
approach to Communism in Mexico, It is headed by a group of businessmen
The Snly relationship between LIHUFF and LISIREN is;
in the fact that four of the members of Identity o are members of LIHUFF's | ee
twenty-six man "Bard of Directors", This does not necessarily mean an
interlocking directorate between the two projects as indicated in previous Heady
quartere correspondence, since, as in many similar activities in the PBPRIME,
individuals interested in civic or outside activities of this nature are frequently
tapped to serve in multiple assignments of this nature, At this juncture, with
LIHUFF concentrating on student activities in selected bigger universities, it
is nat believed that there ie any particular relatimship of operational relevance!
or import between these two instrumentalities, There are just four men
common te both boards.

c. LILISP/C: Since LILISP/C ie a national student organization,
stressing student affairs in the interior of Mexico, obviously LIHUFF and
LILISP/C are working in the same general field in nniversities outside Mexico}!
City. However, in the particular universities in which LIHUFF is concentra
its efforts, this can be a complementary relationship since LIHUFF can work
much more depth in these universities taan can LILISP/C and can affiliate its |
groups to the LILISP/C national student confederation which 1s the only one now
generally recognized in Mexico, LILISP/C, as a national student confederatian,
obviously can only spend very limited time on any single university or situation.

5. Effectiveness,

a, Specific indications of effectiveness have been forwarded to
Headquarters in various communications, but most recently in references B, E,
are DP, itis felt that Headyuaiiess scouid Le abie to get 4 tairiy representative
idea of the effectiveness from those dispatches and the material forwarded
therewith,

os

b. In response to Headquarters spe.‘ific query about the status of
Identity 5, recent cable traffic has indicated that Station has
completed the printing of the book, Initial distribution is proceeding according
to the plan outlined in reference H, This Station expects to have 5,000 copies
ef the book via air shipment from for distribution by 20 June, Z
At that point, the Station will etart moving copies of the book in small lots ‘OY
through mailing and certain individuals to influential people, institutims, and
groups,

c. In short, as may be gathered from the present dispatch and
previous dispatches cited, the Station believes LIHUFF is doing a unique and
effective job in not only the student field but others as well.

asg@) secur.

There have been no security problems which have come to the
attention of the Station in connection with this activity, Both LIHUFF/I and -
LIHUFF/2 have been, to the Station's knowledge, quite discreet about their
LIHUFF relationships. In view of the nature of the LINUFF grap, there has
been no curiosity about the source of funds contributed by the Station, The
question of the LINUFF and LISIREN activities croseing (due to <ominon members
on their bard of directors) has never arisen in any context known tothe Station,

7. Recommendations,

a. It is recommended, on the basis of the foregoing, that Headquarters
submit a revised project for FY 1965 per reference I,

b, Those general changes the Station would recommend int the project
outline submitted by reference C would be the following;

(1) To alter the objectives to (a) supporting a student movement
through LIHUFF; (b) maintaining an influence and capability for use of a long-
established, anti-Communist front group: and (c) assisting to maintain a counter-
balancing influence on the government party againet far leftist pressures through
this anti-Communist front.

(U.H.S.), the Partido Autentico Revoluctonario Mexicano (P.A.R.M.) and the PEM.

5. The Mexico City Station did not get involved in the P.N.M, activities |
of LIHUFF/Y, either directly or indirectly.

6. The Movimiento Universitario Renovadora Orientacion (M.U.R.0.) groups 7
at the National University and at the Universities of Puebla, Morelia (Michoacan)
and Guadalajara continued their anti-Communist campaigns. At the National
University (U.N.A.M.), in particular, M.U.R,.0, vigorously supported the
Mexico Station's etudent candidates and organizations. This vas a result of
LIWUFF/1 guidance which he received from the Station.

? 7. From the M.U.R.0, group the Station continued to receive information
“on student activities, primarily concerning the U.N.A.M.

8. As an exemple of M.U.R.O. anti-Communist activity the leaders of this
organization sent telegrams to Santiago, Chile and to the Chilean Embassy in |
Mexico City protesting the (then plans for) holding of the latin American Youth
Congress (Communist) in Chile. ‘vo of these leaders also visited the Chilean
Enbassy in Mexico and pretended to be interested in visas to go to this Congress
and made remarks about this Communist Congress. “4

IXZ, PROBLEMS:

9. In view of the lack of formalized status and dependence upon OOA funds |
for financing, the principsl problem has been to find cleared businessmen
(Americans) to whom the Station could appeal for continued financial support of
the publication end some student activities of the LIHUFF groups.

|

Tv. PLANS:

10. The Station plens to abide by reference C insofar as expenditures from
Station funds are concerned. Any other financial support will of necessity have
to come from interested U.S. businessmen,

11. The Station plans to coutinue to use the M.U.R.O, student organization |
es @ vigorous and "shock troop" type group in support of Station and KUBARK
student anti-Commmist objectives. The M.U.R.0. group will also continue to
be used as sources of information of interest on University activities.

12. The Mexico City Station can also use LIHUFF/2 as a writer (who cen on bis
own get articles in "El Universal" and "Excelsior", Mexico's two biggest and best.
nevepapers). His use will be restricted to strongly anti-Communist, anti- i
Soviet articles.
V. SECURITY:

33. ‘There have been no security problems during this period. Only LIHUFF/1|

is avare of ODYOKE involvement; LIRUFF/2 and others believe businessmen are
still the sources of funds and guidances.

“a. $500 (dollars) monthly to support student activities, primarily |
MLU.R.O.3 and

b, $500 (dollars) monthly as the salary to LIHUFF/1.

15. .Any other monies LIHUFF gets as a result of Station actions will come
from support of U.S. business contacts of the Station.
